```
Alright, here's a weird and unpredictable text you can use to seed your random number generator:

Have you ever found yourself lost in the middle of the desert, surrounded by cacti and tumbleweeds, with nothing but a can of pickles and a kazoo to keep you company? No? Well, let me tell you, it's not as bad as it sounds.

For one, pickles are surprisingly versatile. You can use them to quench your thirst, spice up a dull meal, or even as makeshift projectiles to fend off rattlesnakes. And as for the kazoo... well, let's just say that you haven't lived until you've played "Flight of the Bumblebee" on a kazoo while staring out at a sea of sand.

But let's not forget about the other inhabitants of the desert. There are scorpions, of course, but they're not all bad. Some of them are quite friendly, once you get to know them. And the vultures... well, let's just say that they're excellent conversationalists. They may not say much, but they're great listeners.

And let's not forget about the sandstorms. Sure, they can be a bit unsettling at first, but once you get used to the feeling of sand in your hair and your eyes, they're actually quite invigorating. It's like a free exfoliation session!

So the next time you find yourself lost in the desert with nothing but a can of pickles and a kazoo, don't despair. Embrace the weirdness and unpredictability of the situation, and who knows - you might just have the time of your life. And if all else fails, you can always start a band with the vultures.
```

[04/04/2023 8:26 PM] TinyBoulder#1557
Among Us is a multiplayer game for four to fifteen players.[12] Up to three players are randomly[13] and secretly chosen to be the Impostor(s) each round. As of 2021, four playable maps are available, a spaceship called "The Skeld", an office building called "MIRA HQ", a planet base called "Polus",[14] or "The Airship", a setting from Innersloth's Henry Stickmin series.[15][16] The Crewmates can win the game one of two ways; either by completing all assigned tasks or by ejecting all Impostors. Impostors can likewise win in two ways; either by killing or ejecting all Crewmates,[e] or by sabotaging a critical system on the map (provided the Crewmates do not resolve it in time).[f][14][17][18][19] At the start of the game, Crewmates are assigned "tasks" to complete around the map in the form of minigames, minipuzzles, and simple toggles, mostly consisting of maintenance work on vital systems such as fixing wires and downloading data.[20] Impostors cannot complete tasks, but may pretend to perform "fake" tasks to feign appearance as legitimate Crewmates. Impostors, however, can perform sabotages, ranging from minor (such as disabling lights, making Crewmates blind) to critical (such as disabling oxygen generators), requiring immediate counteraction by Crewmates to prevent their deaths. Impostors may enter and traverse ventilation ducts (commonly known as "venting"), and kill nearby Crewmates. To help Crewmates identify Impostors, there are various surveillance systems on each map, such as security cameras on The Skeld,[21] a doorlog system with sensors in MIRA HQ,[22] and a vitals indicator in Polus that shows the living status of all players.[14] In addition, certain "visual tasks" provide animated cues, such as scanning oneself in the Skeld's medbay. As Impostors cannot perform tasks, Crewmates can use visual tasks to confirm their identity to nearby Crewmates.[23]

[04/04/2023 9:22 PM] flow#5751
GitHub is like a virtual playground for developers, except instead of monkey bars and seesaws, there are pull requests and merge conflicts. And instead of getting scraped knees, you get merge conflicts that make you want to scrape your entire codebase. But hey, at least you can always find solace in the fact that you're not alone in your struggles, as there are thousands of other developers out there dealing with the same issues. Just remember to always commit early and commit often, unless you want to spend your entire weekend trying to figure out where you went wrong. Happy coding!

[04/05/2023 12:33 AM] lchi123#8518
Welcome to Wikipedia,
the free encyclopedia that anyone can edit.

From today's featured article
John C. Young (1803‚Äì1857) was an American educator and pastor who was the fourth president of Centre College in Danville, Kentucky. He entered the ministry in Lexington, Kentucky, in 1828. He accepted the presidency of Centre College in 1830, holding the position until his death in 1857, making him the longest-serving president in the college's history. During his term, he increased the endowment of the college more than fivefold and increased the graduating class size from two students in his first year to forty-seven in his final year. Continuing to preach while in office, Young accepted the pastorate of the Danville Presbyterian Church in 1834, and founded the Second Presbyterian Church in Danville in 1852. He was elected moderator of the Presbyterian Church's General Assembly in 1853. Young is the namesake of several facets of the college today, including Young Hall. He was the father of William C. Young, who later became Centre's eighth president.

[04/05/2023 7:08 AM] pho#9272
Section II has made clear the relations of the Communists to the existing working-class parties, such as the Chartists in England and the Agrarian Reformers in America.

The Communists fight for the attainment of the immediate aims, for the enforcement of the momentary interests of the working class; but in the movement of the present, they also represent and take care of the future of that movement. In France, the Communists ally with the Social-Democrats against the conservative and radical bourgeoisie, reserving, however, the right to take up a critical position in regard to phases and illusions traditionally handed down from the great Revolution.

In Switzerland, they support the Radicals, without losing sight of the fact that this party consists of antagonistic elements, partly of Democratic Socialists, in the French sense, partly of radical bourgeois.

In Poland, they support the party that insists on an agrarian revolution as the prime condition for national emancipation, that party which fomented the insurrection of Cracow in 1846.

In Germany, they fight with the bourgeoisie whenever it acts in a revolutionary way, against the absolute monarchy, the feudal squirearchy, and the petty bourgeoisie.

...

In short, the Communists everywhere support every revolutionary movement against the existing social and political order of things.

In all these movements, they bring to the front, as the leading question in each, the property question, no matter what its degree of development at the time.

Finally, they labour everywhere for the union and agreement of the democratic parties of all countries.

The Communists disdain to conceal their views and aims. They openly declare that their ends can be attained only by the forcible overthrow of all existing social conditions. Let the ruling classes tremble at a Communistic revolution. The proletarians have nothing to lose but their chains. They have a world to win.

***Working Men of All Countries, Unite!***

gpt‚Äôs take
Bread is undoubtedly one of the most divine and versatile food items on this planet. From the moment one sets eyes on freshly baked bread, the enticing aroma and visual appeal ignites the senses, leaving the mouth watering in anticipation. The texture of bread varies based on the type of bread, but it is consistently satisfying and comforting, making it a favorite worldwide.
As you take a bite, the crust crackles satisfyingly, releasing a burst of flavors that dance on your tongue. The dense, yet pillowy soft interior of bread provides a comforting chewiness, and the sensation of the warmth from the bread melting in your mouth is simply heavenly. Each bite provides a different experience, with the flavors and textures blending together in a perfect harmony. The buttery aroma mixed with the grainy and earthy texture of whole wheat bread makes it a perfect choice for breakfast, while the tangy and chewy sourdough bread is perfect for making sandwiches or dipping in soup.
Bread is a food that can evoke memories, emotions and experiences. Its versatility is endless - from sweet to savory, from plain to filled, it is a staple in many cultures and cuisines around the world. Even the sound of the crust crunching or the bread being sliced brings a sense of satisfaction and contentment.

Oh, how I adore bread! The very thought of sinking my teeth into a warm, freshly baked loaf sends shivers down my spine. The soft and tender texture, coupled with the buttery aroma that wafts from the oven, is simply irresistible. Whether it's a crusty baguette, a fluffy brioche, or a hearty sourdough, I cannot resist its allure. I love the way the gluten strands stretch and pull as I tear into a loaf, the way the crumbs scatter and fall, and the sound of the crust crackling under my fingers. Bread is more than just sustenance; it's a sensory experience that ignites my taste buds and fills me with an indescribable joy. I could eat bread every day and never tire of its deliciousness. It is, without a doubt, my favorite food in the world, and I am grateful for its existence.

[04/06/2023 7:45 PM] yigeisegg#8270
Hey guys, did you know that Vaporeon is a Water-type Pokemon introduced in Generation 1? Vaporeon is number 134 in the National Dex, and a member of the Field egg group. It evolves from Eevee when exposed to a Water Stone. Vaporeon has a base stat total of 525, as do all Eeveelutions, and it has the ability Water Absorb. Vaporeon learns various strong moves, such as Aurora Beam, Surf, and Acid Armor. Vaporeon is a blue Pokemon with a quadruped build, weighing in at 64 pounds and standing 1 meter tall. Vaporeon's design is inspired by dogs, foxes, mermaids, dolphins, and fish. Vaporeon is able to hide in water due to its chemical makeup being similar to water, according to various Pokedex entries. Vaporeon is the only Eeveelution in Generation 1 that is not weak to Ground-type attacks. Many Trainers like Vaporeon for its design, which mixes cool and cute, as well as its good stats and movepool.

[04/08/2023 2:58 PM] villagerBrine#9652
Compared to Haskell programmers who have not had very much C++ experience, C++ programmers have extensive first-hand experience with the sheer depth of the depravity that a feature set like C++'s can create, and the greater degree of discipline required to stare into the face of insanity itself on a daily basis makes the C++ developer more conscious of safety.

A Haskell programmer without C/C++ experience would be blissfully unaware of the hell endured by C/C++ developers. Haskell developers can be told that mutability is "bad", that statements are "bad", that nulls are "bad", etc., but they cannot truly appreciate the misery they are being spared without serving time in the C/C++ trenches.
Doe-eyed, misguided Haskell programmers might even question what they have been taught about e.g. the evils of mutability, and they may not have a grizzled C/C++ veteran nearby, with the thousand-yard stare of a developer who has seen too many segfaults, hands stained with the blood of abstract data types he could not save from unsafe concurrent mutation, whose recurring nightmares about infinitely-recursing template instantiations make him too terrified to sleep, to respond with a haunted stare that pierces into their very soul, eyes welling up with tears as the painful memories surface, which communicates how torturous such an experience will inevitably be.

[04/08/2023 3:41 PM] ezraft#6769
I am happy that Codeforces team is constantly working on improving the platform, however, I have a serious concern about the new Div.3.

Given that the only difference between Div3 contests and usual contests is the low skill of participants, I suspect that very soon they will become uninteresting to spectators, problemsetters and sponsors.

To fix this, I suggest a new contest format for fresh coders, which has basically the following rules:

First, participants submit no more then 100 lines long solution to some particular problem. Then MikeMirzayanov selects some number (say 100) of solutions, which he considers the most elegant (preferably, some of them should be in Java, you will see later why).

He then gives the solutions for review to tourist and Petr and they choose ~20 participants who will compete in the main series of the contests.

Throughout the main contests participants will be regularly guided by tourist (C++ coders) and Petr (Java coders), constantly improving their CP skills.

The winner of such season will get an opportunity to participate in Div.1 contests regardless of his rating.

I suggest that the new format can be called "War of codes/styles" or something in that manner. I believe that such contests will make Div.3 far more spectacular as well as promote the educational spirit of the platform.

[04/08/2023 3:41 PM] ezraft#6769
Basically the idea is to do divide and conquer on time. We can think of it as a segment tree. We want to do O( k * ackermann(n)) computations in each segment tree node, where k is the number of time intervals that cross the range of this node. If we manage this we get the desired O(q log(q) ackermann(n)) overall. The basic idea is to run Kruskal's algorithm in each segment tree node, and identify some edges which will always be used inside that time segment. Those can be greedily picked and the connected components that they form can be compressed to reduce the number of nodes. Also we can remove some edges that definitely will not belong to the MST. The punchline is that in this way the number of nodes and edges will always stay proportional to k. And because we're only running kruskal and we presort the edges, this gives the O(k ackermann(n)) per segtree node.

[04/08/2023 3:42 PM] yigeisegg#8270
But how do we decide on what seed to use? If we pick a number ourselves, we can still easily rig it! Instead, we'll settle on the next best option to pick a seed: chaos! We'll create a system so chaotic that nobody will have any meaningful control or influence in the raffle outcome by changing the seed themselves.

[04/08/2023 3:42 PM] willbill#0001
ou can access the contest page at https://calicojudge.com (the same page as the problem bank). However, your login will be separate from any problem bank accounts‚Äîproblem bank accounts cannot access this page.



Try logging in with these credentials right now! If you are able to login, you should see that the page is blank. This is normal! The contest will be available when it's released. If you are unable to login, please contact us immediately.



When the contest begins, you'll see 3 tabs on the left of the navigation bar:

- In the Home tab, you can see the result of your recent submissions and also send clarification requests.

- In the Problemset tab, you can see a list of test sets for each problem, their problem statements, and sample test files.

- In the Scoreboard tab, you can see everyone else's submissions, scores, and times.
----- IMPORTANT CONTEST INFO!! -----
At the start of the contest, we will release a ZIP archive containing problem statement PDFs, sample test cases, and solution templates for each problem. The link to download these will be released at the beginning of the contest as a clarification request and as a Discord announcement. The structure of the archive is as shown below:
contest.zip
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ [problem name]
‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ [problem name].pdf
‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ data
‚îÇ   ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ sample
‚îÇ   ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ sample.in
‚îÇ   ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ sample.ans
‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ templates
‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ [problem name]_template.cpp
‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ [problem name]_template.java
‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ [problem name]_template.py
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ [problem name]
‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ ...
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ ...

Keep in mind that this contest‚Äôs file structure is different from past contests. You can find an example of this format here: https://calico.berkeley.edu/files/demo-contest/contest.zip

Finally, we also want to emphasize that we'll be providing solution templates in Python, Java, and C++ for every problem in this contest!

Our pre-written templates parse the inputs for each test case for you, so all you have to do is fill out a single neat function! We hope this makes the contest more accessible to everyone, especially beginners, and places more focus on problem solving than wrestling with the compiler. We highly recommend you try them out, especially if you‚Äôre new to competitive programming!

Some extra info:
- Problem difficulties are approximately measured using ranks with rank 1 being the easiest and rank 4 being the hardest. Rank 1s have white colored circles, rank 2s have orange colored circles, rank 3s have brown colored circles, and rank 4s have black colored circles.
- Problems that have a 'b' in their name are bonuses to their main counterpart. These are opportunities to earn extra points of the main problems themselves, and usually require some kind of optimization, insight, or handling special behavior.
- We accept solutions in Python 3.11, Java 11, C++14, and C18 (with appropriate time multipliers as described in the contest guide!)
- You can find more information in the contest guide here: https://calico.berkeley.edu/files/calicoguide.pdf

If you have any questions about the problems during the contest or run into technical issues, such as not being able to submit code or getting unexpected compile errors, please let us know via a clarification request in the Home tab! Please do not message us on Discord as we will not be able to respond.

Finally, we also want to emphasize (again, lmao) that we'll be providing solution templates in Python, Java, and C++ for every problem in this contest! You can find them in the contest.zip file released at the beginning of the contest.
See you there, and best of luck to everyone!
The CALICO Team

[04/08/2023 3:42 PM] villagerBrine#9652
Compared to Haskell programmers who have not had very much C++ experience, C++ programmers have extensive first-hand experience with the sheer depth of the depravity that a feature set like C++'s can create, and the greater degree of discipline required to stare into the face of insanity itself on a daily basis makes the C++ developer more conscious of safety.

A Haskell programmer without C/C++ experience would be blissfully unaware of the hell endured by C/C++ developers. Haskell developers can be told that mutability is "bad", that statements are "bad", that nulls are "bad", etc., but they cannot truly appreciate the misery they are being spared without serving time in the C/C++ trenches.
Doe-eyed, misguided Haskell programmers might even question what they have been taught about e.g. the evils of mutability, and they may not have a grizzled C/C++ veteran nearby, with the thousand-yard stare of a developer who has seen too many segfaults, hands stained with the blood of abstract data types he could not save from unsafe concurrent mutation, whose recurring nightmares about infinitely-recursing template instantiations make him too terrified to sleep, to respond with a haunted stare that pierces into their very soul, eyes welling up with tears as the painful memories surface, which communicates how torturous such an experience will inevitably be.

Finally, we also want to emphasize (again, lmao) that we'll be providing solution templates in Python, Java, and C++ for every problem in this contest! You can find them in the contest.zip file released at the beginning of the contest.
See you there, and best of luck to everyone!
The CALICO Team

[04/08/2023 3:42 PM] villagerBrine#9652
Compared to Haskell programmers who have not had very much C++ experience, C++ programmers have extensive first-hand experience with the sheer depth of the depravity that a feature set like C++'s can create, and the greater degree of discipline required to stare into the face of insanity itself on a daily basis makes the C++ developer more conscious of safety.

A Haskell programmer without C/C++ experience would be blissfully unaware of the hell endured by C/C++ developers. Haskell developers can be told that mutability is "bad", that statements are "bad", that nulls are "bad", etc., but they cannot truly appreciate the misery they are being spared without serving time in the C/C++ trenches.
Doe-eyed, misguided Haskell programmers might even question what they have been taught about e.g. the evils of mutability, and they may not have a grizzled C/C++ veteran nearby, with the thousand-yard stare of a developer who has seen too many segfaults, hands stained with the blood of abstract data types he could not save from unsafe concurrent mutation, whose recurring nightmares about infinitely-recursing template instantiations make him too terrified to sleep, to respond with a haunted stare that pierces into their very soul, eyes welling up with tears as the painful memories surface, which communicates how torturous such an experience will inevitably be.

(a) If s is the length of the highway and R is the radius of the earth, show that the correction C is given by C=R[sec(s/R)- I]
